:::::::::::::::::::::::::

::::: section1
::: title-section1
[2/2/71](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle168){#e9781466802179_c08.html_title168}
:::

::: p
Is it possible I owe yet a second liberation to Simone de Beauvoir? Twenty years ago, I read [The Second Sex]{.i}. Last night, I read [L'Invitée]{.i}. No, of course. I still have much to live through to free myself. But, for the first time, I was able to laugh. Change the class (most important), age (20 years more experience!), country, and physique of Xavière, and it is a perfect portrait of C\[arlotta\]. I see the entrapment from the outside (the way that self-sacrificing, Christian love is provoked, alongside the sexual passion),---I didn't feel sorry for myself, I despised myself a little less. I ceased, a little more, to hope---and I felt lighter. I could laugh, tenderly, at myself.
:::
:::::

::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[4/11/71 New York](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle169){#e9781466802179_c08.html_title169}
:::

::: p
Joe: Two kinds of people---those who are interested in self-transformation and those who are not. Both require the same amount of energy---it takes as much energy to remain the same as to change.
:::

<?dp n="331" folio="315" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I agree with the first---and I'm only interested in people engaged in a project of self-transformation. But the second: I wish I could believe something so optimistic. It seems to me to require much more energy to change.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Aphorism by \[[the Polish writer, poet, and satirist]{.i}\] Stanisław Jerzy Lec: "When you arrive at the very bottom, you will hear knocking from below."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
What does sylleptic thinking mean?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
... Stravinsky's death this week. I remember when \[[SS's childhood friend]{.i}\] Merrill and I used to debate whether we would sacrifice our lives to give Stravinsky one more year of life---or five. I was fourteen, maybe fifteen.

::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[4/21/71](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle170){#e9781466802179_c08.html_title170}
:::

::: p
<span>
I'm suffering from a lack of intellectual stimulation. I've exaggerated, over-reacted against the academic milieu in which I was completely submerged in my youth. That was an exaggeration. Then, starting with Harriet, I began an equivalent exaggeration in the opposite direction. It has become more and more extreme, so that in recent years I have spent almost all my time with people with mediocre minds.---However \[much\] they pleased me (because they were warmer, more sensual, more sensitive, had more experience of "the world"), they didn't stimulate me. I thought less and less. My mind got lazy, passive. I gained a lot but I also paid a big price. And it's that price now that humiliates me. I find many books difficult to read! (Especially philosophy). I write badly, with difficulty.
<?dp n="332" folio="316" ?>
My mind is stiff. (That's what's causing the trouble with the women's lib essay---more than my depression.)`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Idea for a novella from \[[the Yugoslav writer and dissident politician]{.i} \] Vladimir Dedijer today. "The Suicide Club." A political story, set in Yugoslavia---imaginary small country. New social movement among students (high school, university): suicide clubs spring up. Young people charged with the project of committing "altruistic suicides" to awaken conscience, blackmail government. They have meetings, workshops, consciousness-raising groups to prepare themselves. Then do it. In all there are 24 who do---(some are murdered, lose courage at the end and are pushed by their comrades). Dedijer's son did it at 19---jumped off a cliff just over his father's house. Later, it's discovered that the clubs were organized by the secret police.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Dedijer had 3 sons. First committed suicide at 15, after being interrogated + beaten up by the police (about his father's activities) then sent home---he hanged himself. Second killed himself at 19 (suicide club). Third tried last year---failed---went on the road in US, took drugs, now in an athletic school in Switzerland.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Novella organized as a collection of "material" on the clubs. Like Oscar Lewis' anthropological studies of Puerto Rico + Cuba. Letters, taped interviews, report of researcher ... Ends with researcher trying to leave the country and has his documents confiscated.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Read \[[the French sociologist Émile]{.i}\] Durkheim on altruistic suicide.
:::

<?dp n="333" folio="317" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Use story Florence told me about her father \[[the French writer and politician André Malraux]{.i}\]---at the cemetery, following the interment of her brothers, they walked around and he delivered an impromptu lecture on the history of coffins from Sumerians to the present. Use that---father of one of the suicides; he is a professor or government minister.
:::

::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1

::: p
The density of Ivan Illich comforts me---makes me more present to myself, stronger.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Jeanne \[[the French actress Jeanne Moreau]{.i}\] this weekend: all air. How depressed I was.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I believed in miracles---all my life. Finally, I decided to make one. I failed. I wanted to die.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I knew you have to put your life on the line to perform a miracle. There can be no holding back, no reserve. So I did. And I failed.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The assumption on which I'd based my whole life was finally tested. I---it---failed the test. My life fell down.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Do I build it up? The same way? A better way? Is there a better way? (Without believing in miracles?) Or is "building up" the wrong metaphor?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
It was as if my whole life was growing toward that point I reached two years ago---to be open finally, to be wholly generous, to give myself. I did. I was rejected.
:::

<?dp n="334" folio="318" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I was pure. (Was I?) And I was also grandiose? Was that wrong?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
[BC]{.i} \[[Brother Carl]{.i}\] is about making a miracle. It is the testament of that faith I still had: my prayer, my confidence ... I made the film. Carl succeeded. I failed.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The energy---and the pleasure, the reward---behind the miracle was the longing for symbiosis. A pure, generous dream. But a defective energy.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Am I through with the search for the perfect ideal symbiosis? Is one ever through with a longing so profound as that one?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I am alone. I know that now. Perhaps I always will be.

::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[4/27/71](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle172){#e9781466802179_c08.html_title172}

::: p
Solitude is endless. A whole new world. The desert.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I am thinking---talking---in images. I don't know how to write them down. Every feeling is physical.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Maybe that's why I can't write---or write so badly now. In the desert, all ideas are experimental in the body.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I touch a central place, where I have never lived before. I wrote from the margin, dipping down into the well but never fully gazing down. I drew up the words---books, essays. Now I'm down there: in the center. And I find, to my horror, that the center is mute.
:::

<?dp n="335" folio="319" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I want to speak. I want to be a person who speaks. But, up to now, speech meant dealing in this left-handed, eyes averted way with myself.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I used myself as another person ... Ivan says it's all in \[[SS's essay]{.i}\] "The Pornographic Imagination." (Or [Death Kit]{.i}, I would say.) But I didn't know it. I didn't look down, but rather marveled at those curious, morbid, extreme thoughts I had---and thought myself lucky in not having to pay (in madness, in thickening despair) for being their vehicle. Lucky!
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I was afraid of going mad. Now I've looked---I'm there. I'm not mad. I'm not even depressed being alone night after night in the apartment.

Idea for a novel:
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Look up Paris newspapers, late 1934---Galapagos adventure of baroness and three young men, recounted by \[Paule\] Thévenin ...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Dr. Friedrich Ritter and Frau Dore Strauch von Koerwin arrived at the Galapagos Islands in 1929 to live there---both were Germans. Before coming there they had taken the precaution of having all their teeth extracted---replacing them by "râteliers" of steel. They wanted to create an Eden---which they called Friedo (first syllables of their first names). In 1924 (?) the famous Baroness Basquet von Wagner, accompanied by three very young men, arrived on the island. The total disappearance of the Baroness, who had herself called the Queen of the Galapagos, and two of her suitors; the fortuitous discovery of the third on the beach along with the corpse of a "pecheur de passage" \[["passing fisherman"]{.i}\] made big headlines in the papers toward the end of 1934 ...
:::

::::::: section1

::::::::::::: section1

[5/10/72 Cannes/Cap d'Antibes](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle176){#e9781466802179_c09.html_title176}

::: p
Two films seen here I've learned from, admired. Herzog's TV-STYLE documentary about blind-deaf people \[[Land of Silence and Darkness]{.i}\]. The new Jancsó "about" Attila \[[La Tecnica e Il Rito]{.i}\]---his obsessional meditation about war (armed struggle), power-domination---one of the most erotic films I've ever seen (the eroticism of men). A dream about how a charismatic world-conqueror is created: the psychological elements oneirically reconstituted. The opposite of the analysis made in \[Roberto\] Rossellini's [La Prise du Pouvoir par Louis XIV]{.i}, but equally valid.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p

::::::: section1

[7/5/72 Paris](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle178){#e9781466802179_c09.html_title178}

::: p
A writer, like an athlete, must "train" every day. What did I do today to keep in "form"?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \

::: p
<span>
\[[The American writer]{.i}\] Leonard Michaels at the \[Café\] Flore: He said we looked alike (Russian-Polish-Jewish ...), that what first turned him on to me was that I mentioned \[[the Cuban-American torch singer]{.i}\] La Lupe in the "camp" essay and he went to see her. He wants to write like La Lupe---writing for him is "musical"---the beat. He liked the fucking in the train at the beginning of [Death Kit]{.i}. He thinks \[Samuel Richardson's\] [Clarissa]{.i} is the greatest English novel. "Do you read? I mean do you read a lot?" He thinks the gauchistes are "barbarians." He can't speak French and he never heard of the Flore. He was born at the beginning of January 1933 on the
<?dp n="344" folio="328" ?>
Lower East Side---his father immigrated in the early 20s, his mother at the beginning of the 30s---his first wife committed suicide (in the next room, 47 sleeping pills) while he was a graduate student---his second wife, naturally, is a DAR \[Daughter of the American Revolution\] (his words)---he has two sons, age 3 + 6 ... He went to Music + Art \[[public high school in New York City]{.i}\] \> Univ\[ersity\] of Michigan \> Berkeley`</span>`{=html}

::: p-blanc

::: p
I am invited to China for three weeks, starting Aug\[ust\] 25.

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
A China book? Not [Trip to Hanoi]{.i}---I can't do the "West meets East" sensibility trip again. And I certainly have no intention of recounting my actual trip. I'm not a journalist. Je ne suis pas raconteur. Je déteste raconter \[["I'm not a storyteller"]{.i}\]. (Unless it is to use the story to illustrate a point---or to be able to analyze + discuss the story afterward + extract reflections from it.)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
What book? Could I do now a "Notes Toward a Definition of Cultural Revolution"? Probably I'll get to see very little of the C\[ultural\] R\[evolution\]. (How could I? I'll never be alone. It will probably be mostly visits to factories, schools, museums). But the idea is there.

:::

::: p
Recount story of film. My father. The China in my head as a child. The "book" on China for Miss Berken's 4th grade class that was the first long thing I ever wrote. The Chinese furniture in the house in Great Neck \[New York\]. Mr. Chen.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
Opening: "I was, as far as I know, conceived in China (in Tientsin, in 1932), but since my parents returned to the United States for my birth (in New York, in 1933), I spent the first years of my life---in the United States---making up for their disappointing prudence by telling school friends that I was born in China. They had gone back to China soon after I was born in New York, and stayed there most of the first five years of my life. My father was a fur trader; he had an office in New York, in the fur district (231 W 31st St), at the head of which he put his kid brother Aaron---and he ran the main office of the company, in Tientsin, which is where he and my mother had lived most of the time since they married in 1930. My father died in Tientsin while the city was under bombardments (it was the time of the Japanese invasion) but of TB on Oct. 19, 1938. He had been born, the fourth of five children of a poor immigrant family on the Lower East Side in New York City on March 6, 1906---had started public school in 1912, at the age of 6, quit school in 1916, at the age of 10 to go to work as a delivery boy in the fur district, and made his first trip to China in 1932, by then a representative of the fur company he worked for at the age of 16. He went into the Gobi Desert on the back of a camel to buy fur skins
<?dp n="346" folio="330" ?>
from Mongolian nomads. He was eighteen when he had his first attack of TB."`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Dedicate book to my father.
:::

::: p
For Jack Rosenblatt (b. New York 1906---d. Tientsin 1938)---"Daddy"---a set of photographs---a boy, as I think about him now---an unfinished pain, Death, the Great Disappearance. My son wears your ring. I don't know where you are buried. I weep when I think of you.---You keep getting younger. I wish I had known you.
:::

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[7/21/72](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle180){#e9781466802179_c09.html_title180}
:::

::: p
<span>
Telling Nicole \[Stéphane\] today how the whole story of [Death Kit]{.i} came in a minute---fell into my lap---the whole histoire: the train, Hester, Incardona, the business conference, the hospital, the return to New York---huis clos \[["closed hearing"]{.i}\]---
<?dp n="351" folio="335" ?>
the entry into the land of death.---everything, on the mention of that mysterious word "Diddy" by John Hollander at the beginning of our midnight coffee date at the Tant Mieux, that now-defunct coffee house on Bleecker Street where I used to go all the time. "What did you say?" "Diddy---Oh. Excuse me. I mean, Richard \[Howard\]. I always forget. That's what he was called in Cleveland, when he was a child." "Diddy?" "Yes." "How do you spell it?" "I don't know. D-id-d-y, I guess." And all the while, [Death Kit]{.i} was filling my head---and I asked John to excuse me, I couldn't stay. I had to go home. I was expecting a long-distance phone call---and I rushed home at 12:30 and began to write [Death Kit]{.i}---the opening part, Diddy & his life, his suicide attempt---in a fever until six in the morning ...`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Telling that story today to Nicole, the story of how the novel was given to me, intact, in a flash, all on the mention of the word "Diddy"---because Diddy has nothing to do with Richard Howard, is in no way even remotely based on him---it was just the word, a kind of "coup de foudre" \[["love at first sight"]{.i}\] à la \[[the French psychoanalyst Jacques]{.i}\] Lacan for that word qui a tout déclenché \[["that unleashed everything"]{.i}\]---but why? [Why]{.i} that word? I've never \[understood\]---telling Nicole that tale, as I've already told it thirty times in the last five years (remembering, as I told it, more my other tellings than the actual event)---suddenly, today, in a flash---again a flash---I understood. After five years, I understand. (And why today?)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Why Diddy? If John Hollander had said his nickname was Bubu or Toto---or Dig? No! Diddy, Diddy only. Those five letters. Why? I've never understood. Today \[I\] saw.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Diddy
:::

::: p
Daddy
:::

<?dp n="352" folio="336" ?>

::: p
That's the source of the meditation on death I've carried in my heart all my life.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Diddy is 33 years old. So was Daddy when he died.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Did-he? Did he die? The theme of false death, la mort équi-voque, la résurrection inattendue \[["unexpected"]{.i}\] in all my work---
:::

\

:::: blocktext
::: p-br-blocktext

Lena (but it fails) in [Brother Carl]{.i}
:::

:::

::: p-blanc

::: p
The resurrection of Lena fails because Susan did die. The manner of her death---and Karen's dream of her resurrection---are taken from that pain. (I ended by not shooting the actual suicide, and cutting the dream!) I had Karen's dream. I told it to Diana \[Kemeny\], who responded as Martin does.
:::

 \

<span>
In the first notebook for \[Dostoyevsky's\] [The Idiot]{.i}, it was Prince Mishkin who killed Natasya Filipovna, not Rogozhin.
<?dp n="353" folio="337" ?>
`</span>`{=html}

::: p
Four days a year perhaps, I have "visits"---things come. Visitations, rather than inspirations. I live the rest of the year on that---executing the orders + sketches I've taken down ... I turn myself into a commodity. The typewriter is my assembly-line. But what else could I do?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \

::: p

::: p-blanc

::: p
\[William\] Hogarth: everything is exteriorized. A person's face is his character [and]{.i} his social status [and]{.i} profession. Everyone is 100% what he is ... Balzacian conception of his own work: paint (dissect, show the conflicts in, unmask the hypocrises of) a whole society. Painting that you have to "read" (a defect?). Cinema. Themes: conflict; hypocrisy; sensual excess.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Antonioni's [L'Eclisse]{.i}---his best film, a great film. All \[[the French writer and filmmaker Marguerite]{.i}\] Duras is there---but so much greater, richer. The Bourse scene is worthy of Eisenstein. Between \[Alain\] Delon + \[Monica\] Vitti, the second half of film: a huis clos ambulant, dehors \[["walking closed court, outdoors"]{.i}\]. Delon (a really professional actor; opposite of \[Jean-Paul\] Belmondo, all charm) sets the rhythm---the way he moves, never stops moving.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
A good listener: a physical presence that is warm, alert, intelligent---more important than any words.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Proust is not Balzac plus all the rest. Balzac was Balzac plus all the rest! The social portraiture plus the theories about society, love, genius, personality---pages and pages of stuff in Balzac just like Proust on time, Proust on recognition, Proust on the \[connection\] between homosexuals and Jews.
:::

a subject: the phenomenology of ideology

\[On Wagner's\] [Die Walküre]{.i}
:::

::: p
... [Incest is instant eros]{.i} (like homosexuality)---the erotic couple of the first act are brother + sister, the erotic couple of the last act are father + daughter
:::

::: p
Some of what is wonderful to listen to in [Walküre]{.i}---orchestral passages w\[ith\]o\[ut\] singing---becomes de-valued when one [sees]{.i} the opera. Then the music suddenly becomes just the accompaniment or illustration of the actor's gestures: like staring longingly.

::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[7/28/72](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle181){#e9781466802179_c09.html_title181}
:::

::: p
It's not true that the ideal situation would be that [every]{.i} person be an artist (gauchiste-utopian cliché) \[anymore\] than it would be desirable that every person be a scientist.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
What would the world do with all those [things]{.i}?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The universalization of art \[would\] be an ecological disaster. An idea of infinite productivity.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
No better than the idea of infinite inventiveness (technology) or the infinite acquisition of knowledge. Concept of [limits]{.i}.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Fear of engaging in "élite" activities is what makes people say that, ideally, everyone should be \[an\] artist.
:::

<?dp n="355" folio="339" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
But some activities are possible [only]{.i} if a few people do them.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The only sense in which everybody could be an artist is if art were understood exclusively as [performance]{.i}---or throw-away art. Art would be something people did, and if it resulted in an object you wouldn't have to (perhaps even be able to) keep it, store it in a museum. Cage, therefore, has a right to say he wants everybody to be an artist. There's very little product-making in his notion of art. There's nothing to keep, monumentalize. It self-destructs.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
To repeat: it's an ecological problem.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p

Recycling one's own life with books
:::
:::::::::::::::::

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[11/6/72 Paris](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle188){#e9781466802179_c09.html_title188}
:::

::: p
Idea for a short story or novella (from a visit of \[[the film producer]{.i}\] Lise Fayolle and her husband Claude Breuer chez Nicole last night):
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
A man---handsome---42 years old---born in Brussels, brought up in Montreal. A writer. Drinks. Long hair. All the clothes he wears have been bought by women. A raté \[["failure"]{.i}\]. Knows "everything." Doesn't keep anything---possessions, old manuscripts, journals. Has worked very little---occasional journalism, free-lance PR photography (John Lennon and Yoko at Colombe d'Or at Cannes Festival in 1970), script doctoring. Published his first novel two years ago; brought out by a small independent publisher in the Alpes-Maritimes, Robert Morel---a modern building in the middle of 180 hectares on the top of a hill ... with one steel door "that closes like a safe"; printed 10,000 copies---all sold, but only in the South of France---not one copy in Paris (publisher refuses to send the books to Paris bookstores, even when they are ordered); \[[Une Journée un peu chaude]{.i}\]; won a small, prestigious literary prize, le Prix Roger-Nimier. Has finished second novel, started on third. Has quit Robert Morel---"it was painful"---"I love him"---letter: "Cher Robert, Je vous quitte. Claude." \[
<span class="i">
"Dear
<?dp n="360" folio="344" ?>
Robert, I am leaving you. Claude."`</span>`{=html}\] No explanation, no expression of regret. "He's pleasing himself. Why shouldn't I please myself?"---"It's for the most stupid of reasons. I want to be able to walk into a bookstore in Paris and see how my book is doing." Now he has an introduction (via \[[the French novelist Françoise]{.i}\] Sagan) to \[[the Paris publishers]{.i}\] Flammarion and to Grasset, one of whom will take his second novel. And he has 100 pp. of the third.`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
He has written all his life, but never had enough "confidence" to publish until 3 years ago. Plays, stories, novels. All the old stuff lost, thrown out, torn up.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Married twice---to a Canadian girl, when very young (she demanded fidelity), then after coming to Paris---in \[his\] late 20s, early 30s---Lise! Now lives in St. Tropez with a rich girl named Catherine. House in the pines.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Went to Cornell. Lived for a while in New York.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
From a rich family. (What does father do?) One of four sons. (Is Claude the oldest?) One of his brothers is dead. The third? The fourth, Philippe, is 39 years old and is a Mongolian idiot.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Philippe didn't "speak" until age 6, didn't walk until age 9. "It was I who taught him to walk." The mother is 82 now. Has never left Philippe for one minute of her life. Is capable of tumbling in the garden now, age 82, to make Philippe laugh.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"My mother is a monster."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
He calls Lise "Fayolle" \[---\] "Hey, Fayolle ..."
:::

<?dp n="361" folio="345" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Photograph of Philippe (5' 5", wears thick round glasses, receding hair, short-sleeved white shirt, grey slacks), mother (white-haired), and Claude---dirty, straggly-haired, unshaven.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
1 in 50 children born to mothers age 45 and up are Mongolian; 1 in 2,000 to mothers under the age of 30.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"Mongolian idiot" called, properly, Down's Syndrome.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Claude: "Don't feel sorry for Mongolians. They're not unhappy. They're happy."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
What do they want? "Nothing. They just want to be left alone. To be left in peace."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"C'est le contestataire dans l'état pur. Il [est]{.i} contestataire. C'est le refus total." \[["It's protest in its purest state. He]{.i} is [the protest. It's total refusal."]{.i}\]
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"Everything a Mongolian says is false." It's learned. It's an imitation.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"The refusal begins at conception. The sperm refuses the ovum, the ovum refuses the sperm."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Mongolians are less "affectionate" with each other than with normal people.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
They often have a good memory.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"My mother doesn't understand Philippe. She is his reason for living, he is hers."
:::

<?dp n="362" folio="346" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"If she dies, he would die the same day." Most Mongolians die young. He is one of the oldest alive in the world.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
He \[Claude\] didn't see his mother for 17 years.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"They don't [want]{.i} to talk. They learn to talk because they are forced to." (Not True)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Says that his mother loved Philippe much more than her three other sons or her husband. "He is the strongest."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"One is never bored being with him."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"The novel I'm writing is not about my brother. It happens that I have a Mongolian brother, that's all."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The novel is in the 1st person. "I want to put myself inside the mind of a Mongolian. Describe the world that he sees---that I see as [him]{.i}." A world without "normal" assumptions and structures.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"My mother is not admirable. What she has done is completely egotistical. She should have let him die."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The claw-like grasp of a Mongolian---the spatulate nails---thick neck, raucous voice, rounded shoulders.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Shows rage and displeasure when he feels like it. A cup is to break as well as to drink from.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"I understand my brother."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Mother has founded a school---institution---for Mongolians. But Philippe has always been at home with her.
:::

<?dp n="363" folio="347" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"Maybe I will imagine mental processes in the novel that [aren' t]{.i} true of Mongolians, but I don't care. What's true is what I am capable of imagining."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Mother was 40 when Claude was born, 43 when Philippe (the youngest) was born.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
How to transform this?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p-br
Journal of C.\
or\
Letters between C. and S\[agan\].
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
In journal, could have the reflections he makes on his novel---his brother---his own life. But is he capable of commenting from the outside---e.g. to understand how this project of the third novel is a violent act of revenge against his mother and his brother?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
in writing this novel, he becomes his brother---but he is more intelligent than his brother (that why he denies his character [is]{.i} his brother, or that it matters whether the mentality he will impersonate, render is in fact typical Mongolian mentality)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
---in writing this novel, he becomes his mother---but more intelligent than his mother. He understands Philippe better than she does.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Becoming his mother and his brother, he becomes, finally, stronger than either of them.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
He impersonates Philippe (but better than Philippe) thereby advancing his claim to his mother's love. He becomes, magically, the preferred son.
:::

<?dp n="364" folio="348" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
He replaces his mother in Philippe's love.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
He becomes what he always wanted to be---in his sad, pathetic, "bohemian" style---the perfect contestataire.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
(C. hates to eat or to sleep. Is very thin. Goes to bed usually between 5 and 7 a.m. Drinks, though. ????, all this, alongside the ideal contestation incarnated by Philippe.)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Letter form: could have a voice---a woman, former wife or lover of Claude, a successful novelist who lives in Paris, genre Sagan---say all this. She is lucid, cynical.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
But the letter form makes the story too long. I want it to move fast---as condensed as possible.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Chute ("fall")? Mother dies, and it is Claude who dies right after---not Philippe.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Three themes I have been following all my life:
:::

\

:::: blocktext
::: p-br-blocktext
China\
Women\
Freaks
:::
::::

\

::: p
And there is a fourth: the organization, the guru.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Three (or four) colonies which I administer---and can exploit. Three (or four) rooms that I can furnish.

::: p
Science fiction revisited. The misogyny of Jules Verne (+ Nietzsche)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::
:::::::

<?dp n="366" folio="350" ?>
::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::

[]{#e9781466802179_c10.html}

::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: chapter
::: title-chapter
[[1973]{.b}](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle191){#e9781466802179_c10.html_title191}
:::

::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[1/6/73](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle192){#e9781466802179_c10.html_title192}
:::

::: p
When I was an infant, I think, I already knew I only had two choices: intelligence or autism. Being intelligent isn't, for me, like doing something "better." It's the only way I exist. If I'm not \[being\] intelligent, I hover near being catatonic.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Film to be based on Raymond Roussel's [Impressions of Africa]{.i} (1910). He died in 1933. A funny, poetic, oneiric film (Story hinges on the fete of a theatrical character given on the occasion of a coronation).
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Film on Gilles de Rais.
:::
:::::::::

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[1/7/73](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle193){#e9781466802179_c10.html_title193}
:::

::: p
Perhaps I have begun to think again. It's too soon to tell. I had begun to believe I had lost my mind.---Or gave it away, because it was too heavy.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Can I love someone (N\[icole\]\] and still think / fly?
:::

<?dp n="367" folio="351" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Love is flying sown, floating. Thought is solitary flight, beating wings.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I have to think about what I think. And I'm afraid.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The terrible, numbing loss of self-confidence I've experienced in the last three years: the attacks on [Death Kit]{.i}, feeling myself a fraud politically, the disastrous reception of [Brother Carl]{.i}---and, of course, the maelstrom of C\[arlotta\]
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Films (tentative hypotheses):
:::

\

:::::: blocktext
::: p-indent-inverse-blocktext
The only kind of films I want to do are S\[cience\] F\[iction\]: dreams, miracles, futurology. SF = liberty.
:::

::: p-indent-inverse-blocktext
Any "period" film is reactionary in itself. Example: Proust, [The Go-Between]{.i}, [Death in Venice]{.i} Counter-example: Bresson's [Jeanne d'Arc]{.i}---Why? Because there are no professional actors ... Hence \[[SS's project to adapt de Beauvoir's novel]{.i}\] [L'Invitée]{.i} would have been a reactionary film ... Another counter-example: Rossellini's [La Prise du Pouvoir]{.i} ...
:::

::: p-indent-inverse-blocktext
What about stars? Conscious manipulation of \[Brigitte\] Bardot-image in \[Godard's\] [Le Mépris]{.i}
:::
::::::

\

::: p
Essay on violence in cinema:
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Compare: 1) eye of woman in Odessa steps sequence (\[of Eisenstein's\] [Potemkin]{.i}); 2) eye being cut in \[Buñuel's\] [Un Chien Andalou]{.i}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
\(1\) arouses compassion, doesn't brutalize; (2) brutalizes. Ken Russell's [The Devils]{.i} comes from (2). A steady progression
<?dp n="368" folio="352" ?>
since [Psycho]{.i} in habituating audiences to endure sadistic assaults without flinching ([Psycho]{.i}, [Repulsion]{.i}, [The Music Lovers]{.i}, [The Devils]{.i}, \[Sam\] Peckinpah's [Straw Dogs]{.i}, Hitchcock's [Frenzy]{.i}). Where is \[[Franju's]{.i}\] [Le Sang des bêtes]{.i} in all this?`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
My position leads to censorship, if it leads to any public action at all. But I can't face up to that. I [can't]{.i} be for censorship.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
[\[SS made a month-long trip to China and North Vietnam in mid-January 1973. I have not found a great many notes from the trip, but much of what was among her papers is reproduced here. Not all of it concerns China directly.\]]{.i}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Cultural imperialism is the key issue. No wonder the US is not xenophobic. It exports its culture---confident it will contaminate (seduce) anyone who touches it.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Current Chinese slogan: "China must make greater contributions to the world." The Chinese modesty about what it can export. China doesn't think it can be a model, not even to the Third World.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
China wants to be left alone. To make a New Zion, need to be isolated. America had that chance. China doesn't, won't.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Calvinist base of American ideology: human nature is fundamentally dark, evil, sinful, selfish, will respond only to egotistical or material or competitive motives
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
Faces with China: either (1) it isn't real (it's a show, it's coerced); or (2) it can't last (wait until materialism gets [you]{.i} (!))
<?dp n="369" folio="353" ?>
Belief that consumer society is the irrefutable seducer (corruptor). Have nostalgia for pristine past of US, but ...`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
How [not]{.i} to use words like:
:::

\

:::: blocktext
::: p-br-blocktext
regimentation\
catechism\
brain-washing\
conformity vs. individualism\
drab
:::
::::

\

::: p
\[[The American sinologist John King]{.i}\] Fairbank has pointed out (in 1971, testifying before \[[the Senate Foreign Relations Committee chairman , Arkansas senator William]{.i}\] Fulbright, p. 38) that American "individualism" translates as "ho-jen-chui," each man for himself, selfishness; "freedom" in Chinese is "tzu yu," means being out of control, doing as you wish, not following your responsible duties, licentiousness
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Self-determination of small groups makes no sense---\[the Chinese\] believe people are one unit, must be unified.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Rituals of mutual aid
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Eating: never help yourself, serve the person to the right + left of you. (Each course in big plate or bowl in the center of a round table.)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Chinese don't understand (deal with) a group that doesn't have a "Chairman."
:::

<?dp n="370" folio="354" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"Culture" in the West, the bastion of the bourgeoisie
:::

\

:::: blocktext
::: p-br-blocktext
culture, a temple\
an elite, its guardians
:::
::::

\

::: p
cf. Nizan book
:::

::: p
In China, for the time being, only [one]{.i} culture---accessible to everyone
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
One iconography:
:::

\

:::: blocktext
::: p-br-blocktext
Mao\
The "\[Gang of\] 4"\
The rev\[olutionary\] ballets\
Art mirrors daily life.
:::
::::

\

::: p
Same repertory---are likely to hear / see it everywhere: a.m. visiting a nursery, p.m. visiting a factory, eve\[ning\] professional Song + Dance ensemble in Sian, Shanghai, or Hangchow
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Women's liberation
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Women // blacks
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
important difference [not]{.i} degree or quantity of oppression (women through most of history have been slaves, chattel---from bound feet, clitoridectomy, immolation on husband's funeral pyre \> no legal status, right to own property, vote, have own name \> abortion laws, job discrimination, etc.) but the fact that they are integrated with their oppressors though in some societies---e.g. Arab, Chinese---women are almost ghettoized
:::

<?dp n="371" folio="355" ?>

::: p
Crucial question: integration or separatism
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Separatism implies at least bisexuality (exclusive homosexuality a result of sexual polarizing---would decline with more integration, abolition of sex stereotyping).
:::

::: p
N.B. Current tendency in movement toward separatism---Redstockings, Gay Liberation Front, Weatherwoman. [Aphra]{.i}, a feminist lit. magazine praised for "not trying to copy male literary standards."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
My own view: pure integrationist.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Aim of women's lib should be the abolition of sex-specific standards for [all]{.i} activities---except child-bearing and, perhaps, a few jobs requiring great physical strength (like coal-mining---but these jobs are rapidly disappearing)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
There may be a "black literature" with its own standards, but there is no "women's literature." Isn't this precisely the old male chauvinist slander. (Cf. treatment of Virginia Woolf) Women do not have---and should not seek to create---a separate "culture." The separate culture they do have is privative. It's just that they should be seeking to abolish.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Only function of caucusing---formation of separatist groups---is transition: to raise consciousness; to lobby.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
[Schools]{.i}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
Why not eliminate schooling between age 12--16? It's biologically + psychologically too turbulent a time to be cooped up inside, made to sit all the time. During these years, kids would live communally---doing some work, anyway being physically active, in the countryside; learning about sex---free of their
<?dp n="372" folio="356" ?>
parents. Those four "missing" years of school could be added on, at a much later age. At, say, age 50--54 everyone would have to go back to school. (One could get a deferment for a few years, in special cases, if one was in a special work or creative project that couldn't be broken off.) In this 50--54 schooling, have strong pressure to learn a new job or profession---plus liberal arts stuff, general science (ecology, biology), and language skills.`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
This simple change in the age specificity of schooling would a) reduce adolescent discontent, anomie, boredom, neurosis; b) radically modify the almost inevitable process by which people at 50 are psychologically and intellectually ossified---have become increasingly conservative, politically---and retrograde in their tastes (Neil Simon plays, etc.)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
There would no longer be one huge generation gap (war), between the young and the not young---but 5 or 6 generation gaps, each much less severe.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
After all, since most people from now on are going to live to be 70, 75, 80, why should all their schooling be bunched together in the first 1/3 or 1/4 of their lives---so that it's downhill all the way
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Early schooling---age 6--12---would be intensive language skills, basic science, civics, the arts.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Back to school at 16: liberal arts for two years
:::

::: p
Age 18--21: job training through apprenticeship, not schooling
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
[\[Undated political note:\]]{.i}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
For \[[the essay SS wanted to write]{.i}\] "Notes Toward a Definition of Cultural Revolution"
:::

<?dp n="373" folio="357" ?>

::: p-blanc

:::

Sartre interview, [New Left Review]{.i} #58, Nov--Dec 1969

::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[3/15/73](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle194){#e9781466802179_c10.html_title194}
:::

::: p
... Where does a writer's authority come from? Where does my authority come from?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Exemplary people, exemplary acts.

::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[7/31/73 Paris](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle198){#e9781466802179_c10.html_title198}
:::

::: p
Maybe I should go on writing stories for two years---fifteen, twenty stories---really clear the deck, explore new voices---before tackling the third novel. Can bring out two collections of stories in the next 2--3 years, re-establish myself (establish?!) as a fiction writer, and create interest---anticipation---in the forthcoming novel.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I'm now writing out of rage---and I feel a kind of Nietzschean elation. It's tonic. I roar with laughter. I want to denounce everybody, tell everybody off. I go to my typewriter as I might go to my machine gun. But I'm safe. I don't have to face the consequences of "real" aggressivity. I'm sending out colis piégés \[["booby-trapped packages"]{.i}\] to the world.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
That's why my voice is getting more American. Because I'm finally handling / touching autobiographical material directly. The Europeanized voice ("tranlatorese") of the earlier fiction was the just correlative of the fact that I had transposed---displaced---what I was writing about.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
It started with the Paul Goodman essay---feeling grief, and having the courage (and interest) to advertize it. The second step was when I thought, in October, that the China trip was
<?dp n="377" folio="361" ?>
cancelled. I was so disappointed---and, above all I didn't want to waste (not have the opportunity to use) all the personal fantasies \[[In the margin]{.i}: (Daddy, M. \[[SS's mother]{.i}\], my childhood)\] that had been stirred up at the prospect of that trip. I wrote a story that started "I am going to China" precisely because I then thought I wasn't. I decided to let the four-year-old have her say, since the thirty-nine-year-old wasn't going to get to find out about Maoism and the Cultural Revolution. (Of course, when, in January, I did get to go---it was the 39-year-old who went; the 4-year-old, to my surprise, didn't even deign to come along. Was it because she'd gotten the load off her chest? No---probably she would never have come---because the real China has nothing, never had anything, to do with her China.)`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The solution to a problem---a story that you are unable to finish---[is]{.i} the problem. It isn't as if the problem is one thing and the solution something else. The problem, properly understood = the solution. Instead of trying to hide or efface what limits the story, capitalize on that very limitation. State it, rail against it.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Freedom of using jump cuts.
:::

::: p
All my life I've been looking for someone intelligent to talk to.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
My mother lay in bed until four every afternoon in an alcoholic stupor, the blinds on the bedroom window firmly closed. I was brought up by a freckled elephant of Irish-German extraction who took me to Mass every Sunday and read me aloud stories in the evening paper about car accidents and loved Kate Smith. At seventeen, I met a thin, heavy-thighed, balding man who talked and talked, snobbishly, bookishly, and called me "Sweet." After a few days passed, I married him. We talked for seven years.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I did my homework with the radio on.
:::

::: p-blanc

And Monday I reserved for Mahatma Gandhi.

Writing like punching somebody

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[12/16/73 Milan](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle206){#e9781466802179_c10.html_title206}
:::

::: p
"Topoi" in letters of Resistance people on the eve of their execution:
:::

\

::::::::: blocktext
::: p-blocktext
forgive me for the suffering I am about to inflict on you no regrets
:::

::: p-blocktext
I am dying for ... (Party / country / humanity / liberty)
:::

::: p-blocktext
Thank you for all you've done for me
:::

::: p-blocktext
I live on in x form
:::

::: p-blocktext
Tell so-and-so that I ...
:::

::: p-blocktext
Once more, I ...
:::
:::::::::

\

::: p
Similarity, no matter what country + what class. (Thomas Mann, in preface to the book \[[Lettere di Condannati a morte della Resistenza europea]{.i}\]---pub\[lished\] by Einaudi in 1954---notes I\[van\] I\[lyich\]'s letter in Tolstoy story.)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Why?
:::

::: p
Need to make a communication that is [efficacious]{.i}
:::

<?dp n="385" folio="369" ?>

::: p
: a) simple
:::

::: p
clear
:::

::: p
no point in subtlety, refinement
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Such a letter is, pre-eminently, a [practical]{.i} communication. Its purpose is:
:::

\

::::: blocktext
::: p-indent-inverse-blocktext
to relieve (reduce) suffering
:::

::: p-indent-inverse-blocktext
to guarantee (shape) posthumous existence, how one will be remembered
:::
:::::

\

::: p
(Perfect text to illustrate Aristotle's [Rhetoric]{.i})
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Nevertheless, some differences:
:::

::: p
difference of degree of \[u\], of personalization, of freedom to express "private" feelings, "sentiments" (least in Albania (+ generally in C\[ommunist\] P\[arty\] members), most in France, Norway, Italy, Holland) difference between Prot\[estant\] + Catholic countries
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Letters are mostly to mothers, not fathers---to wives---to children
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::
::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::

::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[12/23/73 Haramont](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle207){#e9781466802179_c10.html_title207}
:::

::: p
Two shattering reading experiences this year---the correspondence of Flaubert, and (yesterday) the two-volume biography by Simone Pétrement of SW \[Simone Weil\]
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
How depressed I am by both of them---at moments. I feel real hatred for them---because I understand them both so
<?dp n="386" folio="370" ?>
well, because they represent the two poles of my own temperament (longings, temptations). I could be "Flaubert" or "S.W."; I am neither of course---because one side corrects, inhibits, compromises the other.`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"Flaubert": ambition; egotism; detachment; contempt for others; enslavement to work; pride; stubbornness; ruthlessness; lucidity; voyeurism; morbidity; sensuality; dishonesty.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"S.W.": ambition; egotism; neurosis; refusal of the body; hunger for purity; naïveté; awkwardness; asexuality; desire for sanctity; honesty.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
What a painful demystification of S.W. this biography is!
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Her death was a suicide---and she'd been trying to kill herself (notably, by starving herself) for many years.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"I am not a feminist," she said. Of course not. She never accepted the fact that she was a woman. Hence, her making herself ugly (she wasn't), her way of dressing, her incapacity to have any sexual life, her being dirty, unkempt, the disorder of any room she occupied, etc. If she could have slept with anyone, it could only have been with a woman---not because she was "really" au fond homosexual (she wasn't) but because at least with a woman she wouldn't have felt she was being raped. But, of course, that was impossible too---given the time she lived, her particular milieu; above all, the way she had survived implied a profound + irrevocable desexualiza-tion of herself.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
(How lucky I am, since I could very well have made the same "saving" choice as S.W. But I was saved for sexuality---at least partially---by women. By the age of 16 on, women found me,
<?dp n="387" folio="371" ?>
sought me out, imposed themselves on me emotionally + sexually. I was raped by women and I found that not too threatening. How grateful I am to women---who gave me a body, who made it even possible for me to sleep with men.)`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
S.W. of course makes me think of Susan \[Taubes\]. Same hunger for purity, same refusal of the body, same unfitness to live. What was the difference between them? That S.W. had genius and Susan didn't. That S.W. assumed her own desexual-ization, affirmed it, drew energy from it---while Susan was "weak": she could never accept the love of women; she wanted to be hurt and dominated by men; she wanted to be beautiful, glamorous, mysterious. Susan's refusals only weakened her, they didn't give her energy. Her suicide was second-rate. S.W.'s was an exaltation---that's how, finally, she succeeded in imposing herself on the world, securing her own legend, blackmailing her contemporaries and posterity.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
What is left of Susan? A novel nobody read and a manuscript on S.W. that I keep in a closet in NY (unread) whose existence nobody knows.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I remembered last night that in the story about Susan, "Debriefing," I had put in the voice of S.W. at one moment. Quite unconsciously---when I was writing the story in March of this year. Now I understand.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
A lesson: purity and wisdom---one can't aspire to both---they're ultimately contradictory. Purity implies innocence, unselfconsciousness---(even) a certain stupidity. Wisdom implies lucidity, the overcoming of one's innocence---intelligence. One [must]{.i} be innocent in order to be pure. One [can't]{.i} be innocent in order to be wise.
:::

<?dp n="388" folio="372" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
My problem (and perhaps the most profound source of my mediocrity): I wanted to be both pure and wise.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I was too greedy.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The result: I am neither "S.W." nor "Flaubert." The hunger for purity checks the possibility of real wisdom. My lucidity checks my impulses to act with purity.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I am not attracted to suicide---and never have been.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I love to eat, even though it is easy for me not to eat (when no one feeds me, when there is no food around).
:::
:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::

[7/25/74 Panarea \[Italy\]](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle212){#e9781466802179_c11.html_title212}

::: p
"Idea" as method of instant transport [away]{.i} from direct experience, carrying a tiny suitcase.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
"Idea" as a means of miniaturizing experience, rendering it portable. Someone who regularly has ideas is---by definition---homeless.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Intellectual is a refugee from experience. In Diaspora.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
What's wrong with direct experience? Why would one ever want to flee it, by transforming it---into a brick?
:::

::: p-blanc

::: p
Can something be too immediate?:
:::

::: p
Imprisoning.: Too light.
:::

::: p-blanc

::: p
Thinking about my own death the other day, as I often do, I made a discovery. I realized that my way of thinking has up to now been both too abstract and too concrete.
:::

::: p
Too abstract: death
:::

::: p
Too concrete: me
:::

::: p-blanc
 \

::: p
For there was a middle term, both abstract and concrete: women. I am a woman. And thereby, a whole new universe of death rose before my eyes.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \

::: p
I am not trying to control my own death.

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[3/17/75](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle215){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title215}
:::

::: p
<span>
Consider the image of homosexuals in films where that is being subliminally suggested while at the same time being contradicted:
<?dp n="395" folio="379" ?>
for example, many of the roles of Clifton Webb, Edward Everett Horton, and George Sanders in films of the 30s and 40s. Seeing Preminger's [Laura]{.i} (1944) again, I was struck by the fact that the character played by Webb (who turns out to be the murderer) is clearly the portrait of a homosexual: sarcastic, cold, elegant, worldly, smart, an aesthete and art collector.`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
[\[Marked only as "Note from May 1975."\]]{.i}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Problematic essays from the 1960s for me---now---are "One Culture + The New Sensibility" and "On Style." Reread them, rethink the problems.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I don't want to go back on my public association with the new arts, the new politics. But how would I formulate those tastes / ideas today?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Sensibility vs morality?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Not that I have changed my point of view. Objective conditions have changed.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
My role: the intellectual as adversary. (So now, must I be adversary to myself??)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
In the early 1960s, the going ideas were conformity, middlebrow culture, certain kinds of inhibitions. So the aesthetic positions I took were good + necessary. Also, when the focus of political activity was (rightly) against the government + the war---the role of political adversary was right, indeed inevitable, if one had a conscience.
:::

<?dp n="396" folio="380" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
But, in the early 1970s, when the abuse is quite different---abuse of ideas of [liberation]{.i}. Now, ideas which came out of specific situations \[of the 1960s\] are junior high school norms ... What status do those ideas have?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Genius of American capitalism is that anything that becomes known in this country becomes assimilated.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I was never taken in by the politics (pretensions to revolutionary potential) of the counter-culture. In the Cuban piece (1967) I already warned against that.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
---political mistake of the New Left (ca. 1967) was to think you could invent gestures (styles, clothes, habits) that would really divide people. Like: long hair, Navajo jewelry, health food, dope, bell-bottomed trousers.
:::
::::::::::::::::::::::::::::

::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[5/16/75 NYC](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle216){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title216}
:::

::: p
One has the feeling of having lived through an old script. Fellow-travellers of other people's revolutions: French, Russian, Chinese, Cuban, Vietnamese.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Cf. \[[the American social critic Christopher]{.i}\] Lasch's book, [The American Liberals and the Russian Revolution]{.i}.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Perhaps for the last time? "Right" and "left" are tired words.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
The Movement harbored at least three different tendencies: the liberal one, the anarchist, and the radical one. And the radical one has as many themes in common with the extreme right as with the extreme left---so much that is New Left / gauchiste rhetoric being indistinguishable from fascist
<?dp n="397" folio="381" ?>
rhetoric of the 20s and early 30s, as so much that is right-wing (e.g. \[[then Alabama governor George]{.i}\] Wallace) sounds like potential left-wing populism.`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Intellectuals played at crusaders and revolutionaries only to discover they were still patricians and liberals. (As kids played at being urban guerrillas and settled for being punks.) "Liberalism" seems a vast, obscure, swampy territory one never emerges from, no matter how one tries---and perhaps never should.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
It is from liberalism that one gets one's passion for justice---and that longing for a juster order in which those freedoms guaranteed by liberalism probably couldn't survive. The problem with liberalism is that it can never have an unambivalent attitude toward revolutions. Finally, it must take a counterrevolutionary position. (The Maoists are correct.) Liberals can, ought to, support the right of national self-determination (the right of other peoples to have civil wars and make revolutions) and oppose our government's slaughtering them. But liberals can't survive under these governments---as we know from the history of every Communist regime, without exception, that has taken power.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
To be an intellectual is to be attached to the inherent value of plurality, and to the right of critical space (space for critical opposition within society). Therefore, to be an intellectual supporting a revolutionary movement is to be assenting to one's own abolition. That's an arguable position: there is a good case to be made out that intellectuals are a luxury, and have no role in the only societies possible in the future. Cf. \[[the American economist Robert]{.i}\] Heilbroner.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
But most intellectuals don't want to go that far, and will retreat from revolutionary fellow-travelling. Cf.: Lasch book;
<?dp n="398" folio="382" ?>
\[[the American editor and writer Melvin]{.i}\] Lasky on English reactions to the French revolution.`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The phenomenon of revolutionary tourism---cf. \[[the German writer Hans Magnus]{.i}\] Enzensberger essay
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Franz Hubmann, [The Jewish Family Album]{.i} (London: Routledge, 1975) 400 photographs
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Writing at full voice
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Paracelsus (1493?--1541)

:::

::: p-blanc

::: p
Cf. Bellow, who has [not]{.i}, for all his talents, craft, intelligence, produced a great body of work
:::

<?dp n="399" folio="383" ?>
:::::::::::::

::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[5/21/75](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle218){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title218}
:::

::: p
My subject in all the fiction I've written, from [The Benefactor]{.i} on: the fiction of thought. The relation between thinking and power. That is, various forms of oppression and repression and liberation ... I can't think of anyone else who has treated this subject fully, as fiction. Beckett, somewhat.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Conversation with Joe \[Chaikin\] tonight. When he thinks about the theatre, he said, he can't think of any reason to work in it, any meaning to what he's doing. Only when he doesn't think about it (i.e. ask himself the question about the meaning, value, importance of his work) can he enjoy the work---and he does. I replied that when one asks oneself a question for a long time without ever getting a satisfactory answer, there is usually something wrong with the question (rather than the answer). One didn't---until the late 19th century---ask for art to justify itself, to manifest its meaning. That was like asking art to be useful, practical. I made the distinction between activities which were slavish, practical---one knows why one performs them: they're useful, necessary, obligatory---and activities which were free, voluntary, gratuitous. If practicing an art belongs in the second type of activity, and that is what draws us to the arts, then it would seem a kind of mistake to be restless and demoralized because we were subsequently unable to justify that activity, because that activity failed to justify itself as belonging to the first type of activity. We would be in the situation of doubting the value (worth) of our activity---work---because of the very quality that drew us to it in the first place: its gratuitousness.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
(Cf. Valéry---vagueness is not only the condition of literature, but of any life of the mind. "But perhaps vagueness is indestructible, its existence necessary to psychic effulgence.")
:::

<?dp n="400" folio="384" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::
:::::::::::

::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[5/22/75](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle219){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title219}
:::

::: p
Kafka on Tolstoy's [Resurrection]{.i}: "You cannot write about salvation, you can only live it."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I want to write a [Moby Dick]{.i} of thought. Melville is right: One needs a great subject.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Intelligence---beyond a certain point---is a liability to the artist. Leonardo da Vinci and Duchamp were too intelligent to be painters. They saw through it ... And Valéry was too intelligent to be a poet.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
A novel about the Jews: Sabbatai Zevi, Portnoy, Hyman Kaplan, Anne Frank, Mickey Cohen, Marx, Ethel + Julius Rosenberg, Trotsky, Heine, Erich von Stroheim, Gertrude Stein, Walter Benjamin, Fanny Brice, Kafka

:::::::::::

::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[5/25/75](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle220){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title220}
:::

::: p
... I must change my life. But how can I change my life when I have a broken back?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
D\[avid\] said he wasn't fooled by my relentless cheerfulness---from the moment I wake up until the second I fall asleep---over the past two years. I read your fiction, he said. Nobody who wrote those stories could be that cheerful, genuinely.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
But I don't want to fail, I said. I want to be one of the survivors. I don't want to be Susan Taubes. (Or Alfred \[Chester\]. Or
<?dp n="401" folio="385" ?>
Diane Arbus \[[the American photographer who committed suicide in 1971]{.i}\].) I read aloud \[to David\] the passage from Kafka---his summary \[[July 21, 1913]{.i}\] for and against his marriage ...`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I feel like Kafka, I said to D., but I've found a system of safe harbors, to ward off terror---to resist, to survive.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I've constructed a life in which I [can' t]{.i} be profoundly distressed or upset by anyone---except by D., of course. Nobody (except him) can get to me, get into my guts, topple me over the precipice. Everybody is certified "safe." The jewel and centerpiece of this system: Nicole.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I'm safe, yes, but I'm getting even weaker. I have more and more difficulty being alone, even for a few hours.---My panic on Saturdays this winter in Paris, when N\[icole\] leaves at 11 in the morning for the hunt and doesn't come back until after midnight. My inability to leave the rue de la Faisanderie \[[where Nicole Stéphane then lived]{.i}\] and go around Paris alone. I just stay there, those Saturdays, unable to work, unable to move ...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The shadow of Carlotta panics me---most of all---because I don't want anything to make waves. I dread being in a state of conflict. Everything I do is designed to avoid conflict.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
The price: no sex, a life devoted to work, to D., to my flagship N., and to bland maternalistic friendships (Joe \[Chaikin\], Barbara \[Lawrence\], Stephen \[Koch\], Edgardo \[Cozarinsky\], Monique \[Lange\], Colette, etc.). Becalmed, observant, doggedly productive, prudent, cheerful, dishonest, helpful to others.
:::

<?dp n="402" folio="386" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Do I really want to have the rest of my life devoted to protecting my "work"? I've turned my life into \[a\] workshop. I'm managing myself.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
reminds me that the safe harbor isn't going to be so safe for much longer. (N's bankruptcy, the inevitability of selling the rue de la Faisanderie.) Then it will be even harder to change anything.---My taste for custodial relationships. Propensity first developed in relation to my mother. (Weak, unhappy, confused, charming women.) Another argument against resuming any sort of connection with C., whom I found so pathetic, deteriorated in Rome this March.
:::
:::::::::::::::::::::::::

::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[6/7/75](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle221){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title221}
:::

::: p
Two texts which put "modernism" in perspective: Voegelin on his letter to \[Robert\] Heilman 20 years earlier re \[Henry James's\] [The Turn of the Screw]{.i}; Isaiah Berlin on Verdi ([Hudson Review]{.i}, 1968)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Talking about fascism, one thinks of the models of the past---the first half of this century (Italy, Germany, Spain, etc.). Most talk about the new variety of fascism that the second half of the century is spawning, which will be lighter, more efficient, less sentimental. Eco-fascism.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
concern for a pure environment (air, water, etc.) will replace concern for a pure race; mobilize masses not on the basis of fighting racial pollution but of fighting environmental pollution
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p

::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[6/12/75](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle222){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title222}
:::

::: p
Read, for the first time, \[Mary Shelley's\] [Frankenstein]{.i}. Astonishing work by someone eighteen years old, much more astonishing than Radiguet \[[who wrote]{.i} Le Diable au Corps [before he was twenty]{.i}\].
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
It's an "education novel"---the dilemma of "l'enfant sauvage" (cf. \[[the French filmmaker François]{.i}\] Truffaut's [L'E.S]{.i}. \[[L'Enfant sauvage]{.i}\], Herzog's [Kaspar Hauser]{.i}) ...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Victor Frankenstein, far from being the mad baron of the \[James\] Whale films, is a petit bourgeois scientist--- ... and Genevan: Smug, complacent, cowardly, vain, self-congratulatory. The hero is the monster---someone driven crazy for lack of love.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Theme of marriage + the family in \[Goethe's\] [Elective Affinities]{.i} + [Frankenstein]{.i}.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Life of \[[the twentieth-century French poet]{.i}\] Olivier Larronde---in [Art & Literature]{.i}, #10. His bedroom hung with astral maps. Monkey. Hermetic poems. Opium. Black curtains.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Connection between [The Benefactor]{.i} + [Death Kit]{.i}: Freud, at the end of [The Interpretation of Dreams]{.i}, seeking to integrate dream elaboration and its particular economy with the psyche as a whole: "Let us simply imagine the instrument which serves psychic productions as a sort of complicated microscope or camera."
:::

<?dp n="404" folio="388" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: verse
"Man runs towards the grave,\
And rivers hasten to the great deep\
The end of all living is their death,\
And the palace in time becomes a heap.\
Nothing is further than the day gone by,\
And nothing nearer than the day to come,\
And both are far, far away\
From the man hidden in the heart of the tomb."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: source
---Samuel ha-Nagid (b\[orn\] Córdoba, 993, d\[ied\] Granada 1056)

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[7/19/75 Paris](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle224){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title224}
:::

::: p
There is an essay---very general, aphoristic---to be written about [speed]{.i}, velocity. Perhaps the only new category in 20th century consciousness.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Speed is identified with the machine. With transport. With the light, slim, streamlined, male.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Speed annihilates boredom. (Solution to key 19th century problem: Boredom.)
:::

::: tableau
  ----------------------------------- -----------------------------------
  Conservative                        Revolutionary

  Past                                Future

  Organic                             Mechanical

  Heavy                               Light

  Stone                               Metal

  Certainty                           Unpredictability

  Silence                             Noise

  Meaning                             Pointlessness
  ----------------------------------- -----------------------------------
:::

<?dp n="406" folio="390" ?>

::: p
From \[[the Italian futurist Filippo Tommaso]{.i}\] Marinetti to
:::

::: p
McLuhan. Contrast Ivan \[Illich\]'s critique of speed.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::

::: tableau
  ----------------------------------- -----------------------------------
  Seriousness                         Irony

  Memory                              Forgetfulness

  Repose                              Energy

  Habit                               Novelty

  Analysis                            Intuition

  Slowness                            Speed

  Sickliness                          Hygiene
  ----------------------------------- -----------------------------------
:::

::: p
How does this fit with fascist aesthetics? Fascism? Riefenstahl?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Genealogy of this idea. Nietzsche, etc.
:::

::: tableau
  ----------------------------------- -----------------------------------
  Nature                              Life-as-theatre\*

  Pessimism                           Optimism

  Sentimentality                      Virility

  Peace                               War

  Family                              Freedom
  ----------------------------------- -----------------------------------
:::

::: p
Relation of all this (Futurism, etc.) to Enzensberger's idea of the industrialization of consciousness. Does Fascism industrialize consciousness?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
One point is that there ... really is a "fascist aesthetics."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
\> Marinetti: "Everything of any value is theatrical."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
<span>
And probably there is no such thing as a "communist aesthetics"---that's a contradiction in terms. Hence, the mediocrity
<?dp n="407" folio="391" ?>
and reactionary character of the art sanctioned in communist countries.`</span>`{=html}
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Official art in communist countries is, objectively, fascist. (E.g. hotels + palaces of culture of Stalinist era, \[[the Mao-era Chinese propaganda film]{.i}\] [The East Is Red]{.i}, etc.)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
But what about Fascism's sentimentalizing of the past? The Nazis made Wagner their official music; Marinetti despised Wagner.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Ideal communist society is totally didactic (the whole society is a school); every consideration governed by a moral idea. Ideal fascist society is totally aesthetic (the whole society is a theatre); every consideration governed by an aesthetic idea.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
This is another way in which aesthetics becomes a politics.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Re "Aesthetic Judgment." It always involves [preference]{.i} (implicit or explicit)
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Is it understood that there are some categories upon which we must not exercise aesthetic judgment? That limitation is a constitutive part of the very idea of aesthetic judgment?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
What happens if we decide we will judge [anything]{.i} aesthetically? Have we destroyed the idea?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
N.B. Aesthetic judgment always involves preference, but preference doesn't always involve aesthetic judgment.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Some can say "I prefer my mother to my father" without suggesting any unseemly emotional distance, a "merely" aesthetic judgment.
:::

<?dp n="408" folio="392" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
But if we imagine someone saying "I prefer the First World War to the Second World War," we would think that wars were being treated improperly, heartlessly---that wars were being treated as spectacles.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
...
:::
::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::

::::::::::::::::::::: section1
::: title-section1
[7/22/75](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle225){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title225}
:::

::: p
Musical thinking. Magical thinking.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Elegiac.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Negative epiphany: Sartre's chestnut tree ([La Nausée]{.i}). Positive epiphany: Augustine's worm, Ruskin's leaf. Few writers now have a real contact with nature. The standard for writing is urban, psychological, cerebral---the bottom has dropped out of the world. Nature in a positive sense is anachronistic, unmodern.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Nuance, discretion, musicality---that's what I'm trying to get into my writing. What wasn't there before. No sensuality. I thought I had to say everything I thought.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Harold Rosenberg: "To be legitimate, a style in art must correct itself with a style outside of art, whether in palaces or dance halls or in the dreams of saints and courtesans."
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
It's the prose of goys \[[non-Jews]{.i}\] like Elizabeth H\[ardwick\], Bill Mazzocco, Wilfrid Sheed, \[William H.\] Gass, + Garry Wills that turns me on these days. No ideas, but what music. Poor Jews!
:::

<?dp n="409" folio="393" ?>

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
I'm irritated with images, often: they seem "crazy" to me. Why should X be like Y?
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
My exasperation when N\[icole\] wanted to play le jeu de la vérité \[[the truth game---a variant of Truth or Dare]{.i}\] the other night. The subject: Christiane. Let me guess, said N. If she were a food? (But she isn't a food.) If she were a car? (But she isn't a car.) If she were a hero? (But she isn't a hero.) Etc. I felt as if my mind were blowing a fuse.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
Similes are something different.
:::

[8/7/75 Paris](#e9781466802179_toc01.html_toctitle226){#e9781466802179_c12.html_title226}

Chinese material

Babeuf, quoting Morelly ... : ... "Society must be made to operate in such a way that it eradicates once and for all the desire of a man to become richer, or wiser, or more powerful than others."

N.B. "wiser" China

::: p
Or is this the subject for a novel? James wrote [The Princess C]{.i}. in the 1880s. Do we know any more than he knew then? Would Hyacinth Robinson kill himself a hundred years later?
:::

There are two subjects for a noble novel:
:::

::: p-br-blocktext
sanctity\
the "problem" of civilization

::: p
Who would a modern Hyacinth be? Is culture still a "value"---after its back has been broken in the 1920s by Dadaism, Surrealism, etc.

::: p-blanc
 \
:::

::: p
\[[In a box at the top of the page:]{.i}\] Cf. preface of \[Théophile Gautier's\] [Mademoiselle de Maupin]{.i}: attack on realist-utilitarian demands of republican journalism---" ... and thus royalty + poetry, the two greatest things in the world, become impossible ..."
:::

::: p-blanc

::: p
When Hyacinth goes to Paris, he doesn't have to deal with mass tourism---the degradation of all the objects he admires. His fellow-workers in the book-binding shop now take vacations in Europe, too.
:::

::: p-blanc
 \

::: p
(Christianity wasn't so good for art either---until it lowered its moral tone, got civilized, pluralistic.)
:::

::: p-blanc

(What happened to great poets like \[Pablo\] Neruda + Brecht when they put their poetry at the service of the people, the demand for social justice.)

::: p-blanc
 \

::: p
[Little Red Book]{.i} \[[of Mao Tse-tung's sayings]{.i}\] teaches that everyone can think but negates the (traditional Chinese) idea of wisdom.

Trilling on [The Princess C]{.i} ... . : "Hyacinth recognizes what very few people wish to admit, that civilization has its price, and a high one."

---China!
